As Albucius begins his words, since he has compiled this book for you as the final work of medicine, by completing it I see that it will be an end to it, and through its explanations and clarifications, it seems fitting for me to complete this treatise on surgery for you.
For surgery is entirely destroyed in our region and in our time, so that the science of it suffers great danger and its tools are lost; except for a few small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which have been misinterpreted and led to error and uncertainty until the meanings of them are closed and the strength and art prolonged.
And it is seen by me that I will bring this treatise to life according to the method of explanation and clarification and abbreviation; and for the forms of the instruments of cautery and the other tools of work as well, with the addition of description, and for the preparation of them, which is necessary.
Moreover, the reason why a good craftsman cannot be found in this time is because medicine is long, and that its practitioner must first be experienced in the science of anatomy which includes knowing the joints and shapes of the members; and having knowledge of bones, nerves and ligaments, and their numbers and origins; and recognizing the arteries pulsating and quiet ones, and the locations for bleeding them.
And as Hippocrates said with his name "art," but in small work, and even more so in the art of the hand.
Moreover, we have already said about that in the introduction of this book; because whoever is not knowledgeable about what I have said concerning anatomy, cannot avoid falling into error, so that many men have died in this way as I have seen often, for some are unskilled in this science and take themselves to be without it and its experience.
For I saw a foolish and experienced doctor make an abscess called scrophilus on a woman's neck, and cut some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed out, until the woman died among those present.
And I saw another doctor who thought he could extract a stone from a man's body, which was in its state, and the stone was large, and it came out and cut through the bladder with it, so that the man died on the third day.
And I called for him to extract it, and saw that due to the size of the stone and the position of the patient he would die as a result.
And I saw another doctor who took payment from a duke of our land for surgery and approached a negro slave who had a broken thigh; and with his ignorance he prepared the doctor, extracted the fracture through the wound, using pulley devices and strong rods, but did not allow the wound to breathe.
And he tied it up according to his desires, and bandaged it, and left it unventilated for several days and commanded that we keep it bound; and thus it became an abscess and led to ruin.
And I was called to it, and prepared to remove the bandage, and achieved calmness and relief from his pain.
But corruption had already set in the member, so that it could not be stopped, and the corruption spread through the member until the patient died.
And I saw another doctor who opened an abscess cancerous and it became ulcerated near some days, until the malignancy of it grew in the lord of it.
The cause of this is because the cancer grows without humor melancholic, so it does not require any special care, but rather that it affects a member which is hostile to everything.
And for this reason, sons, it is necessary for you that surgery be divided into two categories: one associated with health, and the other associated with danger in its greatest preparations.
And I have already tested this in every place of this book where there is danger and fear; therefore it is necessary for you to guard against it and allow yourself to be misled by the foolish, so that they do not find a way to speak and deceive you.
And thus take your weapons with caution and protection of God, and your patients with happiness and firmness.
And use the best method for salvation and praiseworthy success by the grace of God, and leave the terrible diseases that are difficult to cure, and lay aside your fears for that deception in your faith and in your name will not mislead you: for it remains for your glory, and thus in the world and forever among your sanctifications.
Galenus already said in some of his teachings: "Do not treat an evil illness, so that bad doctors do not call themselves doctors."
And you shall have read this book according to three chapters.
Here begins the division of the book, and the first of the first part. The first chapter deals with the feet, their forms of instruments and the ironwork of cauteries, and what is necessary for the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter deals with abscesses and perforations, boils, sores, extraction of pus-filled sacs and similar conditions, all collected and arranged in the forms of instruments.
The third chapter deals with restoration and dislocation, and the cure of twists and similar conditions; a chapter arranged in forms of instruments for the feet.
It is necessary for me to say the qualities of the juveniles of that cautery and its disadvantages, as well as in what situations the cautery should be forbidden.
Therefore, I say that the discussion of the quality of the juveniles of cautery and its disadvantages is a long and detailed one, subtle due to knowledge, and hidden secrets; many wise men have spoken about it, and there is disagreement among them, and I will only touch upon a small part of their discussions, fearing prolixity.
And so I say that the use of cautery applies universally to any matter or materials, except for two situations, which are cases without material.
In the case of dry matter without material, there is disagreement; for some say that cautery is beneficial in this case, while others say the opposite, that cautery is not suitable for a disease characterized by quality and dryness, since the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is appropriate that diseases that are dry and hard should be treated with something that is wet.
And he who says the opposite, that cautery is beneficial in all dry and hard diseases that occur in human bodies, when you compare the human body and its moisture with the nature of fire, you find that the human body burns.
And I say on the basis of this discussion, that I have experienced this myself on several occasions.
However, it is not necessary that I come back over what has already been expounded and practiced in the chapter on cautery by previous exercise, and to know the diversity of human cases and the disposition of diseases in their circumstances, as well as the causes of these, the accidents of them, and the time period for these.
However, in other situations, there is no need for fear, especially in the case of cold and moist diseases, because all doctors are already in agreement about these, and there is no disagreement over the use of cautery in these cases.
And sons, understand that the secret of healing by cautery with fire and the goodness of it is due to the cautery as burning medicine, because fire is simple, the action of which does not spread beyond the member being cauterized but only causes a slight harm to the adjacent member.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches not only the member being cauterized but also the adjacent member and can bring difficult-to-heal disease and prolonged suffering to that member.
However, fire, due to its sublimity and the goodness of its substance, does not do anything unnecessary; and it is already known through experiment and prolonged study in the art regarding the truth of causes; and for that reason, I am excused from the length of my discussion, and if it were not for the fact that it is not suitable for my book at this point to reveal secret hidden aspects about fire and the quality of the operation on bodies and its expulsion of diseases, I would demonstrate a philosophical argumentative explanation, which could help alleviate your suffering.
Sons, understand that they disagree about the time when it is appropriate to perform cautery and pause the best time of spring.
I say that cautery is appropriate in all times, because the disadvantage due to time is submerged in the benefit of what is achieved by cauterization, especially if cauterization is for pain or necessary pains, strong and fistulas, which do not tolerate delay because it is feared that evil will come sooner than a slight harm caused by the passage of time.
Do not listen to your suffering, or sons, they do not consider this except the common people and foolish doctors, for that disease which is cured by cauterization is not always successful and they await a bad outcome.
And the cause is not as they believe for that, because cauterization is not in a place of medicine which alters complexion and dries up the humidity that is the cause of pain.
But the cauterization is unnecessary in medicine, because of its willfulness to fulfill the virtue and effectiveness of its operation and the greatness of its master.
It is possible that the patient's illness may return at some time in the future, depending on the patient's complexion and the location of their illness, as well as its nature, and what has been prepared in their body from excesses, and what has been acquired by them in food and similar causes; otherwise, the illness that receives cauterization is a subtle illness in a few organs with few excesses and humidity, such as cauterization of teeth for pain and similar cases. It is possible that in this case, the pain will not return, but it will be small.
But it is common speech that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine, and it is right-thinking speech, not according to what I understand in this matter, because I believe it is not healing that benefits with medicine or any other reason for cauterization.
The cause is contrary to this; the belief that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine is not when we administer the methods of healing in some illnesses and those medicines do not work, but rather at the end of the illness, they administer cauterization and it improves the situation. Therefore, from here on, it is clear that cauterization is not the last remedy of medicine, not according to the belief which I understand in the common people and the phrases of foolish doctors.
They said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this only because of the equality of gold and the nobility of its substance.
They said that the location of cauterization does not harm, because this is not absolutely true, since I have already proven and observed that it does not do so in some bodies, and cauterization with gold is better than with iron as they said; however, when you cauterize with fire made from gold, it is not up to you, because it depends on the quantity you want for the color of gold, and it prepares to be used; if you adjust it above the fire, the gold melts due to the heat of the fire, and in the fire some layers are produced so that the artisan can carve it with the tool of the occasion.
Therefore, for this reason, caution must be taken when using iron for cauterization; we should do it gently and as accurately as possible in operation.
And I have already arranged this chapter on cauterization according to the chapters, and I have arranged those of the head within the feet, so that I lighten the question for those who seek it.
Chapter One.
This cauterization treats the coldness and humidity that cause the secondary symptom of which there are two causes, one is a sign of scrofula and many rheumatic fluxes, called corissa, from the head to the hairline and eyelashes flowing, and many sleeping, and toothache and gout, and generally of any illness caused by coldness, such as paralysis, sclerosis, apoplexy, and similar conditions in these illnesses.

Approach the wound edge with your thumb and leave it there until the scar from the fire is destroyed. Cure the location with a strong four-drug ointment until it is healed.
They said that when the wound remains open, it is better to get a splint, because it is more beneficial and helpful.

On the cauterization of fistula in the mouth.
When an abscess forms under the uvula or on the palate or between the teeth and you apply a bandage, it breaks, becomes purulent, and a fistula is formed, and if your treatment does not help, you should burn cautery according to the quantity received in the fistula, and place the burning iron in the fistula opening, keep your hand until the hot iron reaches the abscess opening, and at the end do it again once or twice; and cure it with what we have said about treatment until it is healed.
If the pus is separated and healed, that is good; and if not, it is necessary to expose the location and drill the rotten bone according to its location.
Chapter XX.
On the cauterization of teeth and softening of the gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are damaged, and you treat them with medicines but it does not improve, place the patient's head in your lap, and hold the cautery tool of the shape that will come to this purpose, so that you can quickly press the instrument handle on the tooth and insert the burning cautery into the cavity, keep your hand a little away from the patient until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
Then lift your hand, and move the cautery several times according to your desire.
Then have the patient rinse his mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour, then stop it, because a damaged tooth is closed, a softened gum is strengthened and excess moisture is dried up.
Chapter XXI.
On the cauterization of tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to inflammation, or there is an abscess or worm, or treatment with medicine does not help, you should perform cauterization in two ways: cauterize with a cowhide bandage, or cauterize with fire.
Cauterizing with a cowhide bandage is that you take a cowhide bandage and heat it in an iron pot, then take a piece of the heated bandage and wrap it around the end of the probe, immerse it in boiling water, and place it quickly on the painful tooth until it cools down.
Approach that area several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or cloth in the boil mentioned above, place it on the painful tooth, and place the hot iron on top of that until the iron reaches the cavity of the tooth.
However, the cauterization with fire should be done carefully, and there must be some caution when it comes to the ear or iron, for there may be some large growth and the heat of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And approach the hot iron in the desired shape, place it on the tooth and keep your hand there until the cauterization is cooled; do this several times until the pain subsides or on that day or the next.
And it is necessary to press the patient's mouth with good cloth so that they hold it for an hour and spit, and this is the shape of the cauterization.
Cauterize as desired, according to what is possible for you.

Title (capitol). xxvii.
On cauterizing the hernia in the groin.

Title (capitol). xxviii.
On lancing an abscess in the groin with a cautery.
When an abscess or boil occurs in the groin and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the groin or in its membrane, then if it is in the flesh of the groin, the patient will feel heavy and painful without increased pain.
If it is in the membrane of the groin, then the pain is greatly increased and often doctors become tired in its treatment.
Therefore, it is necessary for the patient to lie on his back; and show the location of the abscess with your finger; and heat the cautery that resembles thread, whose shape was previously described on another page. Cauterize the abscess with that and the cautery until the skin is completely burned through to the pus, until it bursts and drains pus.
And care for it with treatment for other abscesses until it is healed.
It is not necessary to use this type of cautery indefinitely, but rather the one studied in the art of medicine for a longer period and in which many diseases have been known; however, it should be noted that sometimes this operation can be dangerous, but still, it should be done if needed.

Chapter XLV.
Treatise on Cauterization for Ruptures.
When there is a rupture in the hernia and the intestine protrudes through the genital area, begin by having the patient abstain from food on their day and use softening substances to ease the fissure of their stomach.
Then follow the patient closely on their bed and command them to keep their lower abdomen covered until it is ready to be exposed or the hernia appears.
Then return to the area and try to identify the rupture on the pelvis bone, marking the end that resembles the circumference of a circle at the uppermost part of the abdomen.
The form of the heated cautery is as follows:
Heat it until it begins to sparkle. Then return the intestine or hernia to its cavity and place your hand over the area to prevent the intestine from coming out.
You have already opened the space between the patient's thighs, placed a cushion under them, another servant on their legs, and another on their chest, holding their hands.
Place the cautery over the marked spot with your hand holding the cautery steady, and insert it into the pelvis bone until you find the middle of the pubic bone; repeat this procedure if you did not reach the bone in the first examination.
Observe carefully the location of the intestine during your cauterization to ensure that you do not burn the intestine so that the patient does not come to death or other serious harm.
You should know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, do not consider your operation a success.
The cauterization of children should be subtle according to their size and age.
Take care of the cautery site for three days with bandages until the scar from the burn has healed.
Care for that area with other ointments until it is healed.
The patient should remain in bed for 40 days until the site and wound are sealed.
Ensure that the patient's food is adjusted according to the duration of their recovery and that the intestine does not come out under the pressure of healing.
When it is time to move the patient after forty days, administer suitable food and medicine, and continue this for another forty days.
Let him be given rest and nourishment in food and drink, with strong remedies, for if this treatment of healing is followed completely, he will recover.
I will describe the treatment for ruptures in other parts of the stomach, and to begin with, let it not be neglected: cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size, so that it is completely closed as the third part of it; and then care for it with what has been said, and not leave it untreated.

And a line is drawn across the width of the tear, and another line above it; then place your hand with a pointed cautery on top of the tear, but the first cauterization should be lighter and better.
Chapter 46.
On the cauterization of twisting.
When an injury or blow causes pain in any part of the body and this pain persists for a long time without improving with medication, it is necessary to cauterize it using a pointed cautery.

If the injury is healed by the first cauterization, that's good; if not, continue to apply the cautery on it; because it is customary for those pains to be points of one member near another, so you must achieve that with cauterization before the patient is healed.

It is sometimes cauterized with one cautery over the bone of the penis and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver.
You should know that the closer you place the cauterizations, the more beneficial it is and more effective; and you should know that the patient does not feel pain in the cautery, as happens with sores, because the body of the person is already anesthetized.
It is necessary that the cauterizations be large or few according to the members and joints as previously described in the tools (instrumentation).

On the treatment of athelia (cataracts) that affect the eyelids.
Cataracts which extend to the eyelids of some people are sometimes moist and dry in others.
Therefore you should have them with tweezers or scissors, and cut them out with an instrument suitable for the purpose, and place a bandage over the area afterwards.

Chapter IX.
Treatment of large swellings that occur on the eyelids of some people.
Swellings that extend to the eyelids of some people are caused by a condition similar in intensity and hardness to large swelling, which is why it is called "large swelling".
This is an accumulation of thick moisture on the upper and lower eyelids.
Therefore the operation is to determine whether the swelling originates from the eyelid and spreads everywhere, in which case it is mild.
Therefore cut it open along the length of the swelling and remove it from all sides with ease until it drains, and then suspend it with tweezers and remove it.
If the swelling is large, you should adjust it with suture, and care for it until it heals.
If it is small, you will not suffer harm from it because the blood in it will restore and nourish it.
If the large swelling is declining inside the eyelid, you should expose the inner surface of the eyelid, remove the swelling with tweezers where necessary, and press it from all sides. If the incision of the eyelid is long, do not attempt it for any reason.
And after the incision, wash the eye with salt water and care for the area with nourishing treatment until it heals.
Chapter X.
Treatment of exophthalmos (protruding eyes) above the eyelid.
Exophthalmos is an inflammation that occurs in the conjunctiva of the upper eyelid, particularly in children, who it aggravates and often leads to their cataracts. They cannot tolerate bright light due to tearing.
Therefore they often lie on their faces all the time and sleep with their eyes closed; and under their lower eyelids there are swollen and inflamed areas that have already been covered by inflammation, and signs of imminent hernias appear in the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers, the hernia comes out through them.
Another method of operation is to make the patient place their head on your lap, and place a cloth over them and apply heat, making a circle large enough to contain all the hernias from all sides, and then placing it on top and pressing it with your fingers to force the hernia into the middle of the circle. Then make an incision in the middle with a scalpel, taking care that the incision is not larger than the one made during a lithotomy.
But in the incision, it is necessary that you cut through the cord entirely until you reach the hernia, because in many cases the hernia can be removed by making an incision similar to a white cyst.
Therefore, remove it with bandages that you have wrapped between your fingers on the outside and roll it back and forth between your right and left hands until it is expelled.
And be careful not to stitch up the incision because, with the scalpel, you may not reach the eye and injure it.
If your artery does not appear at the beginning of the fissure, but you adjust one small piece facilitating its procession (artery), then pull that out as we have said; immerse rags in warm water and vinegar, place them over the area, and press hard using powders.

However, the method of suture is that you add the dissolution of continuity or with needles as in abdominal suturing, or add the dissolution of continuity with pus as you have been taught.

Chapter XXX.

Chapter XL
In which is contained the entire sermon on the opening of abscesses and their treatment.
Abscesses are of many species and various types, as we shall remember from this book. Each type is described in detail herein.
They are diverse in terms of the method of opening and treating them through two methods: one for abscesses that are located inside the body, and the other for those caused by moisture or fluid accumulation.
The second method is applicable for locations where accidents of the body occur, as an abscess in the head is different from an abscess in the buttock; and an abscess in a soft tissue location is different from an abscess at a joint. Each of these types requires its own treatment methodology.
Some abscesses should not be opened, but rather allowed to mature and heal on their own or complete their course of action.
Some abscesses should be drained when they are hard and do not mature on their own, such as those near joints, for an abscess located near a joint will prolong the pain in that area until it is lanced, and can cause damage to the ligaments or nerves of the joint, leading to stiffness of the affected member; or if an abscess is located on a limb, it should not be delayed in lancing it until it has matured, as this could lead to gangrene; or if it is located near the buttock, it should not be lanced before it has matured, since this could cause the spread of infection into the folds within the buttock and create a fistula, or an opening that does not heal. It is important to know when to lance the abscess, and this is when it has matured.
Know that it is matured when there is the yielding of pain and the ceasing of fever, and the decrease in redness and pulse, and the sharpness of the abscess head, and the other signs.
And know how to perform perforation at the place below the abscess and where pus is coming from healing of the prominence.
Perforation should sometimes be through the length of flesh or body, if abscesses are in the parts of the neck or feet, and in places of ligaments, tendons, nerves, arteries; and in the end, in all places that swell where there is no reflection; for in those that are reflected, use perforation according to that member.
But when the abscess is in fleshy places, it is better to perforate it sooner rather than later as long as digestion of the purulent matter is confirmed, thus as we have said; for if you perforate it before that, the pus's course is prolonged and there may be more putridity, and the abscess's lips are hardened and its depth increased.
If an abscess is under the skin or subcutaneous tissue, you should perforate it when necessary according to the thickness of the flesh or body, or according to what that member requires.
And it is necessary to make a small perforation, and in large abscesses a large and wide or multiple incisions according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And in other abscesses where it is necessary to make a surgical incision and open the wound, when this is done, it is said that the wound has been prepared, as with boils and carbuncles.
And of those that are incised with a wound having three angles; and of these is the one where it is incised like a fig leaf of myrrh, as with abscesses in the joints (gout).
And of those where round and crescent-shaped incisions are administered, and similar to these.
But if it is not like the ones described above (superficial boils), you should perforate it with a superficial or flat perforation only.
And when the abscess is large and has collected a lot of pus, you should perforate it and not take out all the pus at that time; having extracted part of it, leave the abscess open for another day, and then extract a larger part, and perform daily observations until it heals.
Furthermore, if the patient is a young child or elderly person in poor health, for the animal spirit often resolves with the release of pus, and the patient may die from it, you should be cautious about these cases.
Take great care with this chapter, and when performing the perforation of these abscesses, avoid pus-producing diseases and consider whether the wound of the abscess is small or a flat incision; if the abscess is large and the fissures of the perforation are numerous, you should wait for them to close on their own.
If in the abscess a piece of the skin is separated or you have concaved it around its circumference, you should close that with old cloth or thread made from fabric, as when you tie bread or herbs, without moisture; and keep it for three days; and then process and care for it until it heals.
But if bleeding occurs during the operation, you should administer warm water and vinegar mixed in a cloth that can be placed on the area of the bleeding and observed for a while.
If the flow of blood persists, then you must administer the regimen and treatment and powder which I have recommended in several places of this our book and division.
If it is in winter, and the place of the abscess is near many nerves, then you must pack powder made of vinegar and oil of caution on top of it.
If it is summer and the places are fleshy, then you must pack powder made of alum water and oil or vinegar and oil, and leave it for three days as I have said, and then you must drain the abscess and cleanse it, and administer the treatment to it that is appropriate until it is healed.
This is what is necessary for the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses universally, but according to the distinction I have already said about every abscess in a particular manner, this is the method of treating it by chapters specifically.

Chapter xliii.
On the incision of the pit of the abscess in the guolary.
The ancients made this incision on the pit of the abscess, and no one in our land has performed it.
And this is the writing of the sermon of those people.
But in men having scrotum, it must be avoided the extraction of the pit, for it is not helpful because all the veins and larger vessels of the patient are nearby.
But in those who have abscesses cauterized in the mouth or scrotum or both ears, when the disease is not in the neck, it must be ensured to perform incision of the pit to avoid the danger that is caused by suffocation.
Therefore, when we want to perform it, we must incise the pit of three or four circles of the scrotum, or a smaller one in the breadth in that which is between two circles according to quantity, and let the incision be in the cavity, not in the cartilage, and this place is suitable for incision because it lacks flesh and its blood vessels are easily accessible.

Chapter 44.
In this section, we discuss an abscess that occurs in the chest wall outside, which is called a hernia of the chest.
The hernia of the chest abscess is a large abscess as indicated by the color of the body, and it is common in women.
It can be either natural or accidental.
In the case of a natural hernia, there is no remedy for it.
The accidental hernia can be of two types, one of which resembles fatty nodes, and the other type resembles an abscess caused by thickening of an artery, in which case there is fear. It is necessary to make a presumption about it only in the case of a small one. Title. Forty-fifth.
On cutting of the types of knots.
Of knots of various kinds and I have already said all their species in the division.
And it is necessary that I distinguish between a knot and an abscess as there may be doubt.
Therefore, I say that an abscess is heat and fever and violent pain that subsides the ebullition of excess fluid; it is a completed rotting that now ceases the fever, the pain, and the heat.
But a knot is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that cystic lump which is in the bag of the bladder.
And according to the color of the body, and it begins like a boil, and is made in the same way as cheese, whether large or small, and there are two types, one fatty and containing moisture, and the colors of the moisture are swollen, as I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a knot, extract it and investigate it at its beginning for the stone that is called intromes, according to its shape which will appear in the chapter that is close to this.
The method of investigation of abscesses and all knots is that you take this stone, introduce it into the moist part that you find in the abscess, and you roll your fingers over it little by little until you know that the stone has penetrated the skin.
Approach the wound with your hand according to the size of the abscess, and extract the contents while considering what is issuing from its trace.
If the moisture flowing out is forgotten, regardless of its color, then you should cut it with a surface incision as mentioned in other abscesses.
If there is no moisture coming out from the abscess's trace, then you should know that it is fat.
Dry over it with a section shaped like this cross: Thus as you have been taught, and suspend it with a thread, and cut off the skin from all parts with ease, and preserve the skin or sac, if possible, over it and extract the pus with the node.
However, if it is torn during the operation, it will not be possible to extract the healthy part, and therefore you should examine whether there is any cause, and then extract it in pieces before anything remains.
But if something remains, either a little or a lot, return the node according to what is more appropriate.
And if you see that a small part remains, then fill the wound with some sharp and corrosive powders and strengthen it, and place a cauterizing plaster over the abscess, and cure it with another healing method until it is healed.
If the node is large, then you should cut both lips of it and treat it with whatever causes healing.
However, if the pulsating vein is opposite or not pulsating, you should cut it and fill the area with boiling vinegar that is triturated and let it rest for two to three days until the plaster dries and the bleeding of the blood stops; then return to incise what was torn from the node.

Chapter 49.
On incision of abscesses that occur due to an artery or a vein.
When an artery is broken and the coagulum that is above it is consolidated, abscesses occur and there are signs to distinguish whether inflammation and abscess are due to an artery or a vein: for when the abscess is due to an artery, it is long and located in the neck of the body; and if you press on the abscess with your fingers, you feel stridor.
And one that is due to a vein is round in the manifestation of the body.
And incising the abscess is an error, especially in the armpits, groin, neck, and many other parts of the body; and it is dangerous, so its treatment with iron must be avoided, and one that is near the edge, or on the head, should be avoided.
But on one that is due to inflammation of the opening of the artery, cut the coagulum section lengthwise; and separate the section with stitches and the artery, and open the tunics until it is exposed.
And place that needle over the other incision and make it penetrate through, and tighten the ligature with a firm double knot at two places - which causes you to be an apprentice in the extraction of two ligatures that are in the temples.
Then punch the place where there are two ligaments with a spatula until blood comes out completely and the abscess is resolved.
Then administer treatment to produce pus until the ligaments fall apart, and then cure it with appropriate care until it is healed.
If it is an abscess caused by vein section, you must have your hand on the abscess with a ligature and administer treatment, then insert the needle at the place where you have your hand, and make it penetrate; and use double thread to pull it out from the other side, and tie the abscess with a good ligature as I have told you in the grape vine ligature of two parts and both ends of the thread.
But if you fear pulling out the thread, insert the needle through the entire abscess first, and tighten your four fingers at the incision of the needle.
Then dry the abscess in a part of it until what is in it comes out, then you incise the excess of the ligature, and leave what is left connected.
And place a poultice on the inflamed part that you have immersed in wine and oil, and administer treatment with warm and wet care until it is healed.
Chapter of the abscess that occurs by twisting of nerves.
Similarly, as abscess occurs in the ligature and vein, so it occurs in nerves when it occurs due to excessive labor or injury, and for similar reasons.
The worst thing is in the locations of the joints or ankles, or in any location where the joints are injured.
It is a severe abscess, and its color is similar to that of the body, and it is in the larger areas of the body, and when it is narrowed with great force, the patient feels like they are stunned.
It is not an abscess in the front of the body, and therefore it should not be ligated, and it is harmful all over, and does not spread to the sides neither in front nor behind.
Therefore, those who are in the joints should not be sewn with iron, because a strong blow will cause contraction.
But those who are in the head or forehead should be ligated with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, you can use forceps and excise it cautiously.
And if it is large, you should suspend it with an uncini and excise it, then close the wound and care for it until it is healed.

Chapter 12.
Treatment of the umbilicus in an emergency.
The navel is treated for various reasons: either due to a fissure of the navel which exposes the intestine or hernia as in other ruptures; or due to bleeding that flows from veins or arteries as previously mentioned, or due to constricted ventositas within it.
If it is due to a fissure of the navel and exposure of the intestine, then the color of the abscess is similar to that of the body; it is less painful, and different treatments may be applied. If it is due to the exit of the intestine, place that area with something that has been recounted earlier, with a greater degree of diversity, and as you press it with your fingers, it becomes hidden; then return it; and strong heat is applied to that area, and the wound should be cleansed with much effort.
If it is due to moisture, it is less painful and not hidden when pressed with the hand, neither constricted nor swollen.
If it is due to bleeding, darken the abscess by applying these signs:
If it is due to rotten flesh, the abscess is severe, large and hard, and should be packed according to a certain amount.
If it is due to wind, the touch of that area is less painful.
The operation in that area should be considered if the umbilicus is due to bleeding from an artery, vein, or wind; you must be cautious of treating it, for there is fear and danger as taught in the chapter where abscesses caused by arteries and veins were discussed.
If the umbilicus is due to intestine or hernia, you should command the patient to empty their bowels and remain extended; then place your hand around the entire umbilicus, and command them to stay facing upwards between your hands; then circle the area of the umbilicus with a thin spatula; extend the size of the abscess towards the navel's edges with great force; and tie it in the circuit of the umbilicus with strong thread or cord, and use a proper technique for tying.
Tie the middle of the extended abscess to the ligament and introduce the pointed instrument into that area as indicated and try to push the intestine back into its place; if you cannot find or hold it with the ligament, then you must extract the hernia and forcefully push the intestine back into the abdomen.
If you have found the hernia, take it with one hand; and incise any excess tissue from that area.
If it is against your artery or vein, then encircle that area and return to your operation; take two needles and tie them with strong thread and insert the needles into the circuit you have created around the abscess in a cross pattern, making the needles penetrate; and tighten the abscess in four quarters over the needles.
If you wish, remove the needles and allow the extended flesh to fall back on its own; or incise that area which is thin and may be easily closed, and care for it with something that is suitable for wounds until it heals.
If the umbilicus is due to rotten flesh in that area or moisture, you should follow the steps as previously mentioned and extract the pus or moisture from that area, which you will then hold in place, and care for it with something suitable and that consolidates the area.

Chapter LVII.
On the purification of children and on the treatment of those who suffer from circumcision.
Circumcision is not a cure for continence like other diseases: but because it is our operation and theirs by our will, and the removal of that part is specifically in children, it is necessary to assign the best procedure and the easiest method possible without harming their health.
Therefore they did not write about circumcision in any of their books, because it was not used in their laws, and it is only because we have acquired it by experience, the cause being that I have found that most craftsmen and barbers use circumcision and purification with a new knife and torches; and they use liniment and incision with the nail.
And I have already prohibited all these methods and I do not find a better purification with scissors, liniment, or needle in circumcision like with the nail because many times the skin is torn more than before because the foreskin has two layers and one layer remains behind, and it is easily punctured again and certain pain occurs. And the purification that is performed by alphecats and is called digital, which is used by shoemakers, is not secure for the incision of the tip of the male member because it easily enters the wound.
But in circumcision with the nail, a sharp knife can cut and spoil your operation. And the skin of a child is naturally short and many times it does not need purification in that manner because there is no need for it, and I have seen it myself.
But the purification that is performed with scissors and liniment with a needle has been found by me to be bad, because scissors are of proportional incision, so the sharpness above is equal to the sharpness below; and therefore when you press your hand in proportionately two sharp points, and cut it accordingly according to a comparison in one time; and compression of the liniment with a figure containing the skin of the penis from all sides, with which there can be no error at all.
And the method of the first operation is that you keep the child lying down more if he is one of those who are small, that you do not make him stand up except when you put the needle in his penis and let it go the next day.
And make sure that he is happy in every way possible with whatever understanding he has of this procedure. Make sure that he is positioned between your hands and not in the center; and hide the scissors in your hand or under your foot so that the child does not see them or any of the other instruments.
Insert your hand into the penis of the child and inhale the skin, pull it out until the head of the penis is exposed, and then purify that part which has become dirty with filth.
The form of the forceps is modified, this is its shape:
Let the unarticulated ones be not-cutting and the others be cutting, so that the nail does not pierce the flesh, and let the length of both be as sharp as the length of two handles together.
But the mistake in modification is that it forces out completely the internal plaster or you must make an incision.
Therefore, you should stretch out the one with your nail in front of the abscess and make an incision according to its size.
And if you cannot hold it with your nail, then extract it with a tweezers and make an incision.
But if it lasts for more than three days and remains inflamed after the abscess has opened, you should let it drain pus cautiously, clean it gently, and make an incision according to your preparation.
Be careful of the head of the splinter, as it will not come out with that.
And therefore treat it with the remedy recommended in the powder treatment.
If an incision is made in the plaster to the correct size and the edges are observed, it will not become inflamed.
But treat it with what I have said until it is healed.
Chapter 48.
On the cure of retained urine in the bladder.
Retention of urine in the bladder is caused by obstruction, caused by stones or clotted blood, or by tumors or abscesses, similar to those mentioned in the methods of treatment in the division.
If it is not dissolved as I have said, and the cause is severe for the patient, then it is necessary to administer extraction with an instrument called a syringe, which has the following form: It should be made of silver and be narrowly conical, as fine as a bird's feather reed and about the length of a thumb and a half, to which there should be a narrow cannula at its head.
The method of emptying the urine by the instrument is that you take the folded needle and thread it through the wool or cloth for good binding; and insert the extramitatz of the needle into the area behind the syringe, and make an incision with the forceps if any cause requires the wool, but insert it into the cannula forcefully. And move the syringe away from the body and the linen and apply the albumen of egg.
Hold the patient on a hard surface and wrap the bladder and penis with wet oil, olive oil and egg whites.
Insert the syringe gently until it reaches the base of the penis; fold the penis over the pubis; push the syringe into it; and push it further until it reaches the bladder, which should reach the desired result, and not follow this order if it is wrong, but follow the path where it twists.
Then stretch out the penis with a small amount of wool, as the urine will soak the wool.
Then extract it and treat the urine, using a syringe, not ceasing to do so until the bladder is emptied and the patient finds relief.

On the quality of clysters for the bladder with a clamp and similar instruments that are suitable for this.
When ulceration or an abscess occurs in the bladder, or blood clots within it, or it is constricted by a stone, and you wish to distill waters and medicines from that place, then do so with an instrument called a cannula, and this is its form:
If the part of it is mute, it is closed. And in that place there are three passages: two from one side, as sometimes occurs.
At the beginning there is a concave place, in which there is something that is covered, according to its size it should be added, until some cause is drawn from the humors towards that place, it should be drawn, and when it is expelled, with what it is expelled, it should be added, and when it is expelled long, as a cannula is made in naval battles at sea.
Therefore, when you wish to expel humors from the bladder, insert the end of the cannula into the humor, and draw with it the thing that is covered in the opposite parts, because the humor will be expelled into the concavity of the cannula.
Then insert the end of the cannula into the urethra as recommended in the syringe; and draw the humor with what you are drawing, because that humor will reach the bladder immediately, and the patient will feel it.
The subtle crucifix form of the bladder, which is called cystoscopy, and this is its form:
It should be made of silver or copper, the head of which resembles a small feather, and inside it there is a hollow tube.

Then insert the end of the cystoscope into the urethra.

Then tie that in the instrument and proceed as you have done with the bladder, and express it with your hand until the humor reaches the bladder.
Chapter 60.
On the extraction of stones (gallstones).
We have already mentioned in the division the types of stones and their cure with medicines, as well as the difference between stones formed in the kidneys and stones formed in the bladder, and the signs of that.
We have also mentioned the operation on a stone with the hand and the knife.
And the stone formed in the bladder is that which is implanted in the bladder.
And we will now tell it with clear and concise explanation.
Therefore, say that stones formed in the bladder mostly occur in children; and their signs are that urine which is expelled from the bladder resembles water in its subtlety, and appears in sand; the patient strains his abdomen, and passes bloody stools, and it is necessary to press on the lower back in these cases.
The cure of children from this affliction occurs before they have reached 14 years; and it is difficult to cure the elderly. But in young people, it is advisable to use what is appropriate for them.
And of that stone which is larger and the cure is easier; but if it is small, it is contrary to that.
Therefore, when we approach the cure of that, it is necessary at the beginning to cleanse the patient with a cystoscope which extracts all the fissure that is in the bladder; because that fissure sometimes prohibits the emergence of the stone and the search for it.
Approach the patient with their feet and make them lie down in a position such that the stone descends towards the opening of the bladder or occasionally jumps out from its location.
Prepare the patient with your hands and have them lower their clothes, so that the bladder is fully exposed.
Approach and completely expose the affected area.
If you feel the stone in the space, you should immediately make an incision on it.
If the stone is not visible completely, you must anoint it with your left hand's oil if the patient is a child, or your right hand's oil if the patient is a grown man, and insert your finger into their anus. Find the stone and insert your finger to retrieve it. Turn the stone little by little into the neck of the bladder.
Approach and press on the stone with your finger and expel it outward through the incision.
Command the servant to press on the bladder with their hand; command another servant with their right hand to spread the patient's legs apart at the incision site, and command another servant with their left hand to raise the bed sheet that is below the legs, in the location where the incision was made.
Approach and insert an instrument shaped like this: Cut through the area between the anus and genitals, not too much, at the left side; make the incision over the stone and your finger should be in the anus, making a transverse incision so that the incision outside is wide and narrow inside according to the size of the stone that can be possible, and not too wide, for if you press too hard with your finger on the stone, the incision may be difficult; and remember, it is better to err on the side of caution.
Know that some stones have edges and corners, making their extraction difficult because of this.
That stone is round like a peach pit and is easily extracted.
If the stone has edges and corners, adjust it in the groove.
If you are not careful, you must apply pressure on the stone or press it gently but correctly, with a tool whose tip is similar to a file and should be applied to the stone without going astray; or insert a subtle curved instrument beneath it.
But if you cannot apply pressure on it, widen the incision slightly, and if you see bleeding, cauterize it with concentrated vitriol.
But if the stone is more than one, first press your hand to the opening of the bladder and insert your finger; then insert another small instrument near it; proceed similarly if there are more stones.
If the stone is large, ignorance is that you make a large incision, because the patient may experience one of two outcomes: death or prolonged urine distillation, due to which the location is not completely healed.
But administer the stone's removal with care or use forceps to break it into smaller pieces and extract them piece by piece.
When you have completed your operation, fill the wound with aloe and dragon's blood ointment and cauterize it. Place a cloth soaked in oil and vinegar, or rose oil and warm water, on top of it to prevent post-operative infection.
Place the patient on their side and do not remove the linen for three days.
Once you have removed the linen, clean the area with warm water and oil, and care for it with an antiseptic and antibacterial ointment until it is healed.
But if pus, cautery, and corrosive appear in the wound, which resembles blood in the bladder being frozen (and this is known as hematuria), insert your finger into the wound and remove the blood, for if it remains, it can cause the bladder to corrupt and decay.
Clean the wound with soap, water, and salt, and use any appropriate opposition until it is healed.
It is necessary during the entire healing process that you lie down with both legs and adjust the medications placed on the area.
If the stone is small and located in the vagina, and urine flow is prohibited, treat it with what I recommended before proceeding to surgery, for prolonged treatment of this condition can cause surgery; and as I mentioned earlier, take a perforating iron with this shape:
of a triangular shape, sharp, inserted into a rod (or tube)
Then take the iron and tie it to the base of the triangle to prevent it from returning to the bladder.
Then insert the iron into the urethra, penetrating with ease until it reaches that stone. Rotate the instrument slowly in that small stone, and you will perform the perforation on it gradually until the other side penetrates; for the urine is soon released.
Then press your hand on that which is broken from the stone on the side of the urethra, because it is fractured and forgotten by the urine, and the patient is healed.
If this treatment is not possible due to any reason that prevents it, then tie an iron over the stone, and another iron above the stone. Then strike the stone in the urethra between two incisions. Then extract that (the stone). Then remove the ligaments and clean the clotted blood from the wound, which is made in the bladder.
And there is no need for the iron to be tied around the stone, but only so that it does not return to the bladder; and the other ligament on top serves as a precaution, because when the iron is removed near the edge of the stone, it returns to its place and heals the wound.
You are required when you remove the iron from above that you lift the skin over it, or else you will not comply with your obligation, and the wound will heal in this way as has been said.
Chapter LXI.
On the extraction of stones in women.
Stones in women are rarely produced.
If a stone is found in any of these cases, the treatment is difficult and it is forbidden by many methods.
The first one is because the woman who gives birth easily is a virgin.
And the second one is that you will not find a woman who knows if she has been with a doctor when she is a virgin, or belongs to married women.
The third one is because you do not find women who know this craft, especially the operation with iron.
The fourth one is that the location of the incision for stones in women is far from the stone itself, requiring a deep incision, and there is fear in this.
But if the situation requires it, you must take a woman who knows this craft and is scarce.
But if you are deprived of her, then search for one who is experienced and skillful, or present a married woman educated in the affairs of women, or a woman who has mastered this craft in some way.
Therefore present her and command her to do everything that you order her, from the examination of the stone at the beginning; this is because she must determine whether the woman is a virgin, then place her hand in her vagina and seek the stone.
Therefore, if she finds it, extract it from her hand, and then command her to make an incision on it.
But if she is not a virgin, command the married woman to enter her hand into the patient's vagina and examine the stone; place her left hand on the bladder and press it firmly with good judgment.
Therefore, when she finds it, you must gently extract it from the bladder opening on the side and with the assistance of her strength until it reaches its destination at the correct location.
And make an incision on the edge of the hand to determine the location of the stone in any place; the incision should be centered on that side and the incised tissue should not remain attached to the extracted stone.
And the incision should be small at the beginning; then insert the probe into the incision, and if you feel the stone, adjust the incision according to its size, knowing that the stone will be extracted from there.
Know that the types of stones are like seeds: for some are small and large, hard and sharp, long and round, and have rough edges.
Therefore, you know the types of stones because you indicate what you mean about it.
If you see blood flow, adjust the location of the cautery and apply it for an hour until the bleeding stops, then return to your operation when the stone has been forgotten (removed).
And prepare the instruments that are mentioned in the extraction of stones in men, so that you can be assisted by them in your operation.
If you see blood flow and know that the expulsion of blood is due to the arrow that is inserted, then you stop the bleeding with powder on the location and tighten it with pulvils and sutures, and do not repeat this; leave the stone in place and do not extract it, because a woman will die from pain. Treat the wound.
When the wound has become putrid after several days, if it swells up, then return to your operation once the pus is expelled.
Capital sixty-two.
On incision for strangulated hernia.
A swollen hernia is nothing but an accumulation of moisture in the white membrane which contains the intestines and is called the sac.
Sometimes it is in the fatty tissue itself which nature has prepared for this purpose in the separation of the intestines, until it becomes a new intestine; and it is the membrane of the genitals between the white membrane which I have said is not the case.
And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness that occurs in the genitals, so this matter accumulates there; and sometimes it happens by an impact made on the genitals.
And this moisture has different colors; the color of it is either turning yellow or blood red, purple, black and foul-smelling, or white swollen, and this is what is most dangerous.
And the signs by which this accumulation of water is recognized are as follows: if it is in the white membrane that I have said, then the abscess will be rounded and declining a little along its length like an egg-shape, and the genitals appear, since the moisture contains it entirely.
And if the moisture is in the fatty tissue itself, then the abscess will be rounded with the separation of the intestines, and thus it is considered to be another intestine.
And if the moisture is between the membrane of the genitals and the white membrane, cut it with scissors.
And in order to know the color of the moisture, you must examine the color of the moisture within the abscess with a cut made through the center of its shape; and according to what comes out from the interior, judge accordingly.
So when we come to the treatment of it with iron, it is necessary that we command the patient to be lanced if this is possible for you, and sometimes clean the body of him.
Then place a small cushion on his back for some reason and cover him with damp cloths.
Then place yourself on the left side of him, and command the assistant to follow on his right side, who will extend his leg two arms' length to the membrane of the genitals and the lower abdominal wall.
Then take a broad spatula and cut the membrane of the genitals from the same place along its length up to the pubic bone.
Make the incision according to the right angle along the line where the hair of the genitals begins, up to the white membrane containing it.
Remove that, and observe it, and keep yourself for this purpose so that you do not cut into it; and your excision with which you have removed it should be suspended by the largest and most delicate vein, and scrutinize the excision according to its quantity as much as possible.
Then pierce the swollen white membrane with a wide hole and drain all the water.
Then separate between the two lips of the incision with scissors and stretch out the white membrane at its edges; do not touch the membrane of the genitals containing it, and make an incision in that manner as is possible for you. Make an incision of the entire membrane or in pieces, and especially the thinner part of it, because if you do not scrutinize the incision carefully, there is no guarantee that the water will not return.
More if the intestine processes from outside its membrane during the time of your operation, when you have completed the incision of the white membrane, return it inside and then sew together the two lips of the membrane of the genitals with sutures, and treat it in this way as other wounds until it is healed.
And if you find the intestine corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you remove the tools that are its supports and extract the intestine, and treat it as I have said.
However, if the water is accumulated in two parts separately, you must know that there are two hernias; therefore incise the part that you have done on the other side, and if it appears to you that it is a hernia, then you do the operation.
Then you will abstain from blood, enter into the incisions with wool submerged in oil or in oil-soaked wool; and cover another wool which you have immersed in vinegar and oil, and spread it over two genitals and the lower abdominal wall; and cover it with double and thick cloths and linen, and let them lie there according to this pattern:
and place two cloths soaked with carminated wool according to this pattern; the ends of them should be sewn with thread or wet wool, and they should be attached with a structure in the arms of the shirts, and one of the ends will take hold of the buttock up to the back, and the second will take hold at the pubic bone, and two ends on two thighs on one side and two ends on two shoulders, and the entire incision should be sewn together in the arms of the shirts.
And sometimes this hernia is treated artificially with cautery in place of surgery using iron; it is that you take a subtle cautionery knife and insert it into the hernia area near the groin, and it is lit when we have found the white chalk containing water, then you take the cautery as follows: And it resembles Greek letters.
Then pierce that white chalk, and light it until all the moisture is expelled.
Then stretch the white chalk and cut it, remove it with scissors, remove it with a subtle cautery that is lit; and pierce it as far as possible until you eradicate everything; and be careful not to let the fire touch it.
Know that this operation is more safe and distant from bleeding, and better than surgery with cutting.
But if you encounter an abscess at the time of cutting or cauterizing, or bleeding, then you must cure that which opposes you for it, with treatment as appropriate for each case as previously stated.
But if the patient is weak and does not hope for the second operation due to its horror, you must perform perforation as previously recommended; and it is certain that you, according to what I have said about signs, must confirm that this hernia is watery.
You must then place the patient on a raised bed, and pierce the abscess in the lower part of it with a shallow incision, and pause the perforation according to the length of the body.
And the opening should be wide enough for all the water to flow out.
Then pause over the area and let it lie there, so that the remaining water remains. And cure it until the wound is healed.
But if there is resistance to draining the water at that time you perforate it: this should not be done except when the white pus in the wound's orifices creates resistance and prevents the drainage of the water, in which case you must put a pen or instrument with which the water is extracted from the edema, following its design; or adjust in the pressure of the wound a small.
Know that the water returns, and is stopped for about two months or more; and when it has stopped, you must perform perforation according to the aforementioned method, as the patient will pass through their days.
Chapter LXIII.
On incision for fleshy hernia and its treatment.
Know that in incision on this hernia there is fear of danger even in the best arrangements; for which reason I see the abandonment of it and being saved by the better method.
And I remember the operation in that case, and the characteristics of abscesses.
Therefore, it is said that abscesses are formed in bodies composed of genitals and caused by several factors: either by acute aggressive fluid accumulation which is poured into the genitals, or by injury.
Its color depends on the color of the body, and it is not detected in pain, and it is a severe abscess.
A flat abscess is hard, whose color is dark, and it is not felt.
And sometimes it is done by knotting of the arteries, and swelling of those that are already perceived as remembered, or swelling of veins.
But the swelling of arteries is recognized by the dispersal of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it is not necessary to touch it.
But the one caused by swelling of veins is not dispersed by any cause, you must press it with your fingers.
And it is possible that on this type there may be incision and on the other fleshes; and you insert the genitals, and let the water out at the top, and extract it from the white chalk, and release the suspensory ligaments of the vessels, and tie them, and pierce the suspensory that you release from all parts of the water's opening.
Therefore, if the water is already consolidated in those fleshy areas, you must extract the water and pierce it.

But if there is a growth of flesh in the place of adhesion that is behind, you must pierce everything that is from it and extract the water as previously stated.
Therefore, when your operation is complete, you fill the wound with wool soaked in olive oil and wine; and treat it with the other treatment until it heals.

The cure for a hernia is from a root (or plant).

In the treatment of this illness, it is done out of fear for what comes before it (a warning).

Chapter LXV.
On the treatment for internal hernia.
The cause of this internal hernia is a cut made in the expanded cavity over the abdomen of the intestines, because when the intestine ruptures it goes into one of the bowels.
And this rupture can be from the cavity or the extension of it, and both types occur for various reasons: blows, falls, shocks, loud noises, or due to a heavy cause, or similar reasons.
The sign of this is that it occurs gradually over a long period and not suddenly, it is a boil that extends around the anus because the cavity compresses the bowel.
The sign of this is when it is due to a cut in the cavity, because at first it causes a sudden, intense pain; and the boil appears in various places apart from the expected place, and that is precisely due to the bowel, and the body extends beyond the edge of the cavity.
And in some cases the intestine is forgotten and it is called internal hernia "zirbal."
And sometimes it is made with wind, and sometimes the bowel tears open and this is retained, and it is a grave danger for the patient, and sometimes it causes bad pain and particularly when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of the types of this illness with sharp instruments, fear must be avoided, so it is necessary to avoid hunting in that area.
And the method of this operation is to command the patient to return the bowel with his hand to its cavity if it protrudes into it (the body), and place a cushion on his lower back between your hands, and lift his legs.
And then stitch the belt that surrounds the belt of the testicles at the junctures, and make an incision in the entire length of the belt; and insert two fingers into the edges of the incision as needed to cut the incision with those.
And if the incision is large enough that some part of it can be forgotten.
And remove that cavity where the belt of the testicles is located, until the white hard cavity of each side is exposed.
Then insert your finger into the place where the testicle is located between the white hard cavity, which is below the belt, and between the white cavity and resolve the adhesion that exists behind the testicle.
And place your hand on the belt of the testicles at the sides, and with that extend the white hard cavity on its sides with your left hand, lift the testicle and the white cavity to the side of the incision; and command the servant to extend the testicle and you dissolve the adhesion behind it with complete solution.
And search with your hands that there is no cause of the bowel wrapped in the white hard cavity. But if you find any cause for it, then you place it in the abdomen below (the lower body).
Approach the division below the scrotum for section, from which blood and pus should run as we have recommended in what has been said before.
Approach the wound with wool soaked in oil and wait; then administer the bandage that we have recommended (and sometimes a white linen is cauterized, as we mentioned to prevent bleeding, because often this happens), and leave the bandage until it falls off by itself.
But if the wound heals slowly, boil some water and wrap it around, then wait until it falls off as we have said before.
Approach the wound with another method for treating wounds until it is healed.

Chapter LXVII. (67)
On the rupture that occurs in angina.
