Chapter LXVIII.
On the softening of the scrotum of the testicles.
When the scrotum of the testicles is swollen in some men it is softened with herbs, since the flesh that is between it is softened and the care of it should be observed.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked in its treatment that he make the patient lie according to his side, and incise the entire swollen scrotum that has been softened over the natural scrotum; and then adjust two lips with stitching.
And if you wish, cut at the beginning of the excess swollen scrotum with three or four stitches and with a firm stitch.
Then incise between the stitches, and care for other sores until they are healed and the fields heal up.
Chapter LXIX.
On castration.
Know that castration in our law is forbidden, but there is a reason for me to remember it in this book; and it is not necessary to remember it except in two ways, of which one is when it is in the knowledge of the doctor when he is questioned about it, who knows the cure for it if it occurs; and the other way is that we sometimes have a need for castration of other animals for our benefit, such as horses, cows, pigs, and similar animals.
And therefore, say that castration is done in two ways: either by strangulation or by making an incision and cutting off the testicles.
However, in the castration by strangulation, the method of operation is that we tie up the animal in hot water until its testicles are softened and lined up and hanging down. Then take hold of those with your hand until they have dissolved and do not appear again.
In cases of castration due to a split (fissure) and section, you must have the animal (or instrument) and press the scrotum of the testicles with your left hand.
Then draw together the sutures (suspensors), and make an incision through each hole with one cut.
Then make an incision where each abscess has been cut open. Do not leave any cause on the abscess, but treat it with a fine poultice over the vessels (veins).
This method of castration is better when it is done by strangulation, because strangulation weakens the testicles and causes the animal to lose its desire for sex.
Then heal the wound until it is healed.
Chapter LXX (70).
On the treatment of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men is of two kinds: one where it appears when the space between the scrotum and the testicles is filled, in which case there is a female vulva present with pubic hair.
And some of these [hermaphrodites] have a urinary passage that is located in the scrotum of the testicles.
In women, there is one type: it is such that the female genitalia over the pubis resembles two male testicles, but it is slightly smaller and is divided by a small separation like male pubic hair and two testicles.
The treatment is of three kinds: one for men and one kind for women. It is necessary to cut open the flesh closely so that the poison escapes from it, and then cure it with other treatments for other wounds.
In the second kind of men who have a urinary passage in their scrotum, there is no cure or operation for it.
Chapter XXI (21).
On the treatment of leprosy and excessive flesh in women due to certain causes.
Leprosy is treated naturally and is improved by following certain regulations; but it is sometimes excessive in some women to such an extent that it spreads like leprosy in men and extends into the vagina.
Therefore, you must remove the excess of leprosy with your hand or an instrument and cut it open.
Do not continue cutting, especially near the root, to prevent bleeding.
Then heal it with treatment of other wounds until it is healed.
Newly born flesh is flesh that is produced in the mother's womb until it fills up, and it is called "cauda" because of its appearance; therefore, it should be treated like leprosy, and it should be cut open as we do for leprosy, and healed until it is healed.
Chapter LXXII (72).
On the treatment of jaundice.
Jaundice is when the female genitalia is not perforated or has a small hole. And it can be either natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to an illness that has preceded it, and this is caused by poorly sutured flesh or strangulated bowel or spleen.
It is caused either in the mother's womb, during childbirth, due to a suppuration above or below it, or due to a discharge, and it is forbidden to engage in intercourse, pregnancy, or conception, and it is also recommended that menses be avoided.
The diagnosis of this condition is made by examination of the cervix using forceps or a speculum if the opening is visible; otherwise, you should examine it with your fingers or with light.
If the opening is due to strangulation of the bowel, and it is near the two labiae, you should dig and break it open.
And place your fingers between the labiae and press gently on both sides with the forceps.
The woman should be on her back with her legs spread apart and you should extend the labiae with force until the strangulated bowel is broken and the opening is opened.
And apply cotton dipped in oil to the area and leave it there for a few days to prevent the wound from scarring.
If the strangulated bowel is large and thick, then it is necessary to incise it with a lancet or a myrtle leaf.
If the opening is due to sutured flesh, you should suspend it with an instrument and then incise it.
And these are the medicines that stop blood flow without causing pain, such as opium, dragon's blood, and vinegar, mixed with white wax.
Then insert a broad leaden cannula to prevent the wound from healing lightly.
Hold that for several days and administer warm liquid.
And let it heal with the other cure of consolidation until it is healed.
Sometimes it happens in the greater growth of other fleshes, and then it is necessary to incise them according to this method. However, if it is for cancerous abscesses, do not apply iron in any way to the cancerous abscess which is in the major one.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, tail, and red lump that sometimes occur in women's vaginas.
Hemorrhoids are recognized as the orifices of mottled veins in which blood continues to flow constantly; and old hemorrhoids that have become firm.
And I have already said in the division the types of these and the signs of these, and therefore I will say those that receive treatment and those that do not receive treatment.
So I say that hemorrhoids and tumors when in the cervix of the vagina and do not appear to the senses, then there should be no treatment with iron.
However, those that are in the orifices of the vagina which can be felt, are the ones that are cured.
And it is necessary to place the woman in more heat and apply oil of roses or sharp wool, or linen, and incise them with a lancet.
And apply powder over those (hemorrhoids) to stop the blood flow from one of the incisive powders without pain, such as opium and similar ones.
And apply hot water bottles to her feet for an hour, and then place that in cold water.
And if the blood flow continues, then make that sit in a decoction of sumach, mustard seeds, coriander and similar ones.
And apply barley flour with honey and vinegar mixed with water on the anus.
If the blood is separated, it is good; if not, make it adhere with two forceps, and to the nipples without scarification.
And apply wool and immerse it in the juice of colandre, or the juice of arnagleza, or the juice of garlic with repentine vinegar and let it adhere to the place; and let the place be treated with gargles until it is healed.
And let it heal until it is healed.
Chapter LXXIV.
On the perforation of a septic abortion in the uterus.
Different types of abscesses that occur in the uterus, such as cancer, abscessed lapis, ulcers, bladder stones, fistulas hemorrhoids, ruptures, and other abscesses. I have already said about these diseases, their types and signs, and the treatments for them in the division.
And it is necessary for me to say in this treatise about cautery abscess that appears in the uterus when it comes from abscesses that are treated with medicine, and if you want to know how the operation of iron is performed on it.
Therefore, you must consider if the pain of the abscess in the patient begins suddenly with blows and chills and fever, and sometimes it swells and if you can feel that over it, then do not operate on it with iron, but let it heal with water that helps in the maturation of the disease until the acuteness of the accident ceases.
Then you must make the woman lie on a stretcher that has two stretchers; and she should recline on her back and place her feet near the lower abdomen, her thighs spread open, her arms placed under her breasts, and each one in its appropriate position.
And the midwife follows the doctor to the right side and administers the instrument with which the cervix of the uterus is opened, the shape of which will come according to those cases that make it necessary.
And it is necessary that when you want to administer this instrument, you should be in the same position as the cervix of the uterus of the woman, and whatever goes into the uterus from the instrument should not exceed the cervix of the patient. However, if the instrument is larger than the cervix of the uterus, it is necessary to apply powder on the texture of the cervix of the uterus so that the introduction of any instrument into the cervix of the uterus is prohibited.
And it is necessary to let the liquid that flows out of the instrument of the doctor go above and for the one who ministers to hold the instrument and turn the liquid into it until it is opened the cervix of the uterus.
When an incision appears, it is touched with the hand and lanced, then it is necessary that you cut off its head with a lancet.
When the pus is drained, it is necessary that you plug the wound with a plaster soaked in warm oil or vinegar in which there is some styptic substance, and place a linen cloth on top of the wound at its opening.
When you separate the mother and the afterbirth, place a clean wool cloth soaked in water in which evil-smelling herbs have been boiled on top of the navel.
Then let it be cured for about two days with an enema, which is appropriate until it is healed.
After some days, the navel and the wound are washed with water and salt, and then with water in which rosemary or long-armed asterisk is boiled, and then return to the enema.
If the wound is inside the navel and swollen, it is necessary that you refrain from treating it with iron, having care of it as has been said in the division.
Chapter LXXV.
To teach midwives how to treat ectopic pregnancies when they appear unnaturally according to figure.
It is necessary for the midwife to recognize the figure of natural childbirth by signs, and when you see the woman expelling at the onset of labor and desires to breathe air, and above her is lifted by that which comes out with birth, and hastens the emergence of the ectopic pregnancy, then you know that this birth is according to a natural figure, and its head is the first to emerge, and the second one either attached to it or suspended or hanging from the navel.
Therefore, when you see these signs, it is necessary that the woman's abdomen is pressed so that the embryo emerges gently because if it emerges over its head, the second one comes out with it and is cleaned of superfluous matter with good hygiene.
But if this birth is unnatural and incurable because when the embryo comes out above its feet and the body of it is outside the head of it and its legs are, and one hand or foot. The opening sentence translates to: "Either his head or his hand is turned towards his belly, and he has violently twisted his neck onto his shoulder, and the appearance of his body is not praiseworthy."
The necessary cause is that the midwife be wise and skillful in all those cases, and avoid errors and disappointments.
And you are showing the entire figure of them, and which device is in them for it to be understood by him and be standing upon it.
When the man ejaculates on his head due to natural urge, and he is violent towards the woman and it happens with difficulty, and sometimes the potency of him has already been weakened, then do this seizer, or what women have, and evaporate the semen from him with fenugreek juice and moist oils.
Then the midwife enters between her thighs with a small spatula and cuts the second opening, or dries it up with her nail into which the moisture that is in it flows. Press the woman's belly until she gives birth.
If she does not give birth, then it is necessary to rub her with egg white and fenugreek mucilage with a pumice stone.
And command him to do it, rub him with a rough cloth and make him vomit with the condition, and open his mouth and nose for an hour, because the fetus will be forgotten soon.
If the two heads of the fetus are forgotten at the beginning, then it is necessary that you reduce them gradually with ease. If it does not enter, the woman is made to lie on a stone and lift her feet up, and the stone is moved on the ground; and the woman must be held so that she does not fall due to the concussion.
If the heads are not turned inside out and the fetus dies, then you incise them and extract the rotten part of the fetus or seize the body with cloth and extract it, because it will be forgotten.
When the fetus comes out on his feet, it is necessary that you push them upwards, and then turn the fetus small, and open its mouth, and grab one of its feet and stretch them out little by little.
If it is inside the vagina, then command him to push, and make him vomit with a condition, because it will be forgotten if God wills it.
If it is not forgotten by the water we have recommended, then you return the small fetus little by little into its natural position, because it will be easily forgotten soon.
And if it is prohibited by all that we have recommended, then take egg white and dissolved gum, grind everything well in the mortar, and apply the mixture to the cervix of the woman, at the base of her stomach. And make that seizer in hot water until it reaches the hypogastric region.
And when the parts of him have become softened, then make him inhale myrtle smoke and suspend it upon him. And when the inhalation has lasted for an hour, then you make him seizer on a stone, and make him vomit and open his mouth, and take it out, and press gently on the lower part of his stomach to expel the fetus soon.
The long-term fetus hanging from one of its arms. If there is a reduction of the arm, but if you cannot reduce it, then raise the woman and make her bear down.
And if bearing down does not work, then make her lie on a bed and hit her buttocks violently with a hammer, and administer the medicine that I have recommended with mucilages.
And if the labor has begun, then make the seizer on a stone, and study on the reduction of the arm, and deliver the fetus in its natural position, and make her vomit and command him to push until it is forgotten.
The fetus on the expanded shoulders of its mother, and the opening of it is at her waist. It is necessary that the midwife have hold of the fetus and gently turn it little by little, with ease.
And when it is swollen and hardened, then you pause on the affected area with what we recommend for oil and poultices.
And apply small amounts of the poultice gradually, and when you have made it, then place that pestle on a pestle and command it to be tilted towards the right side, and also command someone to hold it; make it shake with condition. Delivery of the fetus prepared on the side.
When the midwife encounters an obstructed labor using this method, consider, and then you shall incise the second one with your nail as far as it is emptied of moisture.
And if the child is suspended on the face and neck, then you shall incise the navel to ensure it does not become stuck and die.
Then gently push the child into the birth canal until you feel resistance and command the woman to take some breaths, and he shall easily come out if it is God's will.
Birth of twins or multiple children. Know that twins born prematurely are often weak, and sometimes three or four are born, but this is rare and usually fatal; however, it is not unnatural, but rather due to the mother's condition.
Count the twins, regardless of how many there are, a second one, and separate them by cutting the ligament at the navel of each one. Sometimes they are easily born naturally, while sometimes they are born easily due to an unnatural cause, and some are born easily without being washable, as we have recommended.
And if they are difficult to deliver, you must care for them in the manner we have described for treating abnormalities.
And if the mother is thin and skilled in all ways that facilitate ease and subtlety, and delay, and is clever according to each figure prepared by the midwife for the good of the patient.
Recollection of that which forms in the womb from embryos and aborted.
Sometimes the number of pregnancies in a woman can be one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, eight, nine, or even more. However, it is essential to confirm that a woman has had either zero or eleven pregnancies, as this was caused by the measurement of the glorious sages.
And all this requires that the midwife be knowledgeable in understanding which of these is similar to the other and therefore apply it accordingly.
Chapter 66.
On the extraction of a dead child.
When you treat a dead child according to what has been said in the division of medicine and it is not outside of that, and you are convinced that you must use force, then consider whether the woman is of good character and not one of those for whom danger is feared due to the circumstances surrounding her.
The woman must be placed on her left side with her head inclined downwards and her hips raised.
The assistant should hold one leg or tie it to the left side to ensure that the body does not extend during the extraction of the child.
You should moisten the woman's mouth with oils and poultices made from althea, fennel, and other seeds.
You should anoint the midwife's hand with those oils and poultices, you should enter your hand into the woman with ease, and you should surround the area where the fingers will be inserted in the child.
In the appropriate place: then consider whether the child is prepared to be delivered on its head, and you shall insert your fingers in the heels, neck, mouth, palate, under the beard, in the crook of its arm, near the ribs, or beneath the hip bones.
But if it is to be delivered on its feet, you shall insert in the ankles or the middle of the ribs.
It is necessary that you hold the finger with your right hand, and bend its curvature in the location between the fingers of your left hand, and enter your hand with ease and insert the finger into one of the places we have mentioned, until it reaches the desired result.
And place another hand or the third one if necessary on the abdomen of the patient, to prevent distention but not extension according to its natural length.
It should be good all around, in order that the swelling may be alleviated as much as possible, just like it is done when extracting a tooth and rooting it out.
It is necessary for him that what is between [the swelling and the affected area] should be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then it is necessary that the midwife anoint some oil on her fingers and gently massage the affected area and rub the retained part.
Therefore, if the birth is forgotten, the fingers should be pressed into the place that is deeper inside; and do this until everything has been expelled.
But if the hand is outside the other and it cannot be reduced by pressure, then a cloth should be wrapped around it; and extract it until it has all been expelled, either at the joint of the hand or at the coccyx.
And in the same way, do this to the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or it happens that pressure can be applied to the swelling, or water is collected at the head, then insert between the blades of the spine spreader and cut the head and drain the water, or break it with an instrument called "alundat", the shape of which will come in the chapter that follows this one.
Do the same if the fetus is large-headed by nature: and then insert it with an instrument called "algeometre", or take it out with an alundat as mentioned before, and extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is swollen and contracted by the furculum, then it should be cut open until the moisture that is in the feet has been drained.
But if there are no complications and it is not swollen or enlarged, then you should cut the head immediately as soon as it is possible for you to do so.
And if the afterbirth is everted or in the wrong place, then it is necessary that you perforate it to drain the moisture that is in it.
But if the fetus is on its feet, then the extraction of it is easy and the direction to the mother's mouth is easy.
But if the fetus is contracted in the abdomen and feet, then it is necessary that you extract it with a cloth that you will wrap around your hand, and cut the abdomen and feet to let the fluid that is in them flow out.
But if the other limbs are stuck and the head turns, then the midwife should insert her left hand; but if the mouth of the mother is obstructed, then insert your hand in the anus of the fetus and find the head with it, and pull it towards the mouth of the mother, and place a finger or two fingers inside, and pull it with them.
And if the mouth of the mother is obstructed by an afterbirth that is in the umbilicus, then it is necessary not to rub it; instead, administer a moist and oily emulsion. Apply plasters; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on the side, then pierce it if possible; and administer what has been mentioned in the living fetus.
And if that is not possible, cut it into pieces and extract it.
It is necessary to avoid any cause within the second childbirth.
And when you have completed your work, administer what has been said about the treatment of afterbirths that occur in the mother.
And if there is bleeding, then send to a stytic water and administer the other treatment.
And I have seen a woman in the belly of which there was a dead fetus, and above that fire another one observed. After a long time there was an afterbirth in the navel of the uterus; and it swelled so much that it burst into fire, and began to emit smoke.
And I was called to cure it, and treated it for a long time, but the wound did not heal.
Then I applied some powerful plasters with strong adhesive to it, and extracted a bone from it, and after several days, I extracted another bone; and I was greatly surprised because there is no bone in the womb.
And then I thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
And so the wound healed, and many small bones were extracted from it, the woman living in that condition for a long time, but recovering gradually with a slight loss of arm.
And I did not wonder about that, since in such cases there is knowledge and help for the doctor when administering treatment with his hand.
In the shapes of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Shape of the lever used to open the mother:
This is the form of strangulation in which the veins are compressed, at which compression there are two benefits in the extremities of two feet. Perhaps this benefit should be more subtle with a constrictor, and it should be made of ivy or hazelwood stick.
The diameter of each stick should be two fingers and the edge of both sticks one finger, and the length of each is a little over a palm; in the middle of the two sticks there are two adjustments of that same stick which have already been fastened, the length of which is a little more than the width of a palm, and the diameter of each is slightly more than two fingers.
And these two adjustments should be inserted into the mother's mouth to open it with those when you perform the prescribed benefits.
Another similar form, but more subtle and lighter:
Make it from ivy or hazelwood sticks in the likeness of forceps. However, at the end of it (the instrument) there should be two extensions like this, and the length of these extensions is a little over a palm, and the diameter of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the mother with it (the instrument), you should first position the woman on a bed, with her legs raised and apart, and open the space between them. Then place your hand on the instrument in a manner similar to when you forceps compress, according to the width that you want for the mouth of the mother up to which the metal will be inserted.

On the extraction of the second tooth:
When the second tooth is retained, it is necessary to order the patient to hold their jaw open, and then you should command that person to cough, and firmly press your hand on their mouth and nose, and if by doing so it has gone beyond (the tooth), good.
And if not, you should take a woolen cloth and perforate it with a hole, and place the herbs that are used to open the mouth of the mother, such as calamint, chamomile, anise, camomilla, scicadus arabicus, cassia lignea, and santaurea, in that hole. All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water during the tide, and place that one on fire.
Then insert a funnel made of cane into the mother's mouth and keep it in until the vapour comes to the concave part of the womb.
Then let that vomit similarly as we have said, and the second one will come out quickly.
If the treatment remains close and is not evacuated, then command the midwife to immerse her left hand in olive oil or alum solution, and insert it into the cavity and seek the second one (finger), and when you find it, take it out little by little... If it is attached to the mother's anus, then insert the hand as recommended, and when you find the second finger, extract it little by little so that the mother does not suffer severe pain. Then lubricate both right and left hands with ease.
If the mother's mouth is constricted, we have already recommended the treatment with stirring and medication of water with herbs.
If none of the causes we have recommended is forgotten, then be careful not to overdo it in the process of extraction, but what comes out of her must be placed in the woman's vagina and anointed with oil and tetraformula; for it will heat up within a few days and dissolve and be forgotten.
When it becomes hot, the evil authority is raised to the head and stomach, and then it torments the patient; therefore, they should be administered sub-fumigations and appropriate treatments.
Moreover, among the ancients, sub-fumigation with cinnamon and dried figs has already been spoken of.
The shape of the instrument by which the woman is sub-fumigated should be used to retain menstruation and the second one (finger):
Made of metal or wood.
It should be stopped at the thin end inside the cavity and the wide end above the fire, and the sub-fumigation should be placed on the arms of the fire.
It should contain whatever is consumed by the sub-fumigation, and another one follows.
Treatment for an unperforated child's bottom.
Newborn children and those whose bottoms are not perforated, which must be treated with care and attention. Therefore, the midwife should pierce that opening with her own finger; and if not, she should pierce it with a sharp spatula, and make sure not to touch the rectum.
Place some wool soaked in wine and oil over it; and anoint it with oil inside, until it heals.
If you fear that it is obstructed, then pierce a cannula for several days and stop when the child wants to relieve itself.
Occasionally there is obstruction of the bottom due to plague or abscess; therefore, that obstruction should be incised, and it should be treated with what has been said about the treatment and lead.
Treatment for fistulas that occur afterwards.
Fistulas that occur after the delivery are not painful and thick, those that occur near the anus or in the space of one delivery.
It is a fistula or moles.
If the thickening is old and has become damp with white, foul-smelling pus or subtle ulcers, some of these fistulas penetrate.
Those that penetrate are recognized by what comes out of them during discharge and by the odor; and sometimes the patient uses evacuation, and it is beneficial for the worms to come out.
Some of these fistulas occasionally penetrate into the bladder space, and into the muscle of the scrotum; and some of these fistulas penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the knot of the buttock.
That in which a fistula penetrates into the anus and does not penetrate is that you put your finger in the anus, and insert a thin probe of wood or metal into the fistula when it is not turbid.
If it is turbid in that one, then insert a thin probe of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or the hair in your finger.
If you do not feel it from top to bottom and do not perceive any cause of discharge, worms, or odor as mentioned earlier, then you know that it is not penetrating, and you can proceed with the treatment.
When the fistula penetrates into the bladder or muscle of the scrotum, the meaning is clearly that it is urine from that one and the place should be consolidated with medicine.
If it penetrates into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and pain occurs in the area, the sign is that the probe enters if there is no turbidity inside the bone, and pain occurs in the area around the delivery; and it becomes pus quickly; and that treatment does not work, nor is it consolidated with oil.
In all these penetrating fistulas there is no cure, and the treatment of them is the labor and futility of foolish doctors on which they rely.
In that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing with iron is expected, as I have told you, and what I have proved.
The patient should lie between your hands upon his back and raise the legs into the air, with the hips inclined towards the abdomen of the patient, and then you should try to enter the cavity with lead or iron if it is in the fistula, until you know where the probe goes.
And if the patient feels pain around the neck, then you should insert your finger into the neck.
If you feel a resistance while inserting your finger to probe, or if you feel something hard with your finger, then you know for certain that it is penetrating; and do not work on that one, because healing does not exist in it, as we said.
But some may say that it heals in some men too.
And the medicine by which healing is expected in that one also involves igniting cautery thinly according to the size of the fistula, as previously described, and inserting that burning into the fistula until it reaches around the neck; and then you should apply it twice or thrice until you know that all the tissues adjacent to the fistula that are similar to feathers of birds are completely tightened.
And heal that one with bandages wrapped in cotton until all the tightened tissues can be seen, and heal that one with medicines to generate and consolidate flesh, and if it heals, it is good; and if not, then it is not healed within a certain time by another treatment.
And if the probe enters but does not penetrate into the anus with your finger, and between that and the suspected probe which may be of flesh or tissue, and sometimes the fistula is found in the scrotum where the skin surface is healed, then you should dry the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it drying along with the probe, and it should go deep into the fistula until the incision reaches the place where the tip of the probe ends, and through the probe the tissue is released and caught.
And heal those fistulous tissues that are similar to the shaft of a bird's feather and remain without any cause.
But if pus flows out between you and your action when probing those tissues, then burn it with fire or an acute instrument, as cauterizing with fire is useful: it tightens the fistulous tissues, and abscesses the pus through drying of the humors.
And heal that one with bandages wrapped in cotton or in coarse cloth until the wound is covered by scab, and then heal the ulcer with hard flesh generating and consolidating medicines.
And the medicines in which there is stopping and drying: when it is restored, it is healed and you do not fear recurrence.
But if the fistula has entered into the anus and is extended from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and probe it.
And if you feel resistance and it is suspected to be tissue or flesh, and it is close to penetration, then do not operate in that one but by faith and hope.
The cause is administered in one of three ways: either you cauterize it as previously mentioned; or you cut it until you obtain the concavity of it so that it is possible for you to enter and cure it properly; and do not proceed with cutting beyond the scrotum, because if you penetrate the rectum involuntarily, and it causes pain to the patient immediately and without his will; and heal it with what has been mentioned before, which works quickly, or stretch that tissue and clean the pus that dries close to the anus, as previously mentioned, either with a probe or another sharp instrument, and then clean those fistulous tissues in the section below where you can with percrustation; and finally, force yourself to restore the entire ulcer with cutting, and if the abscess pus is not consolidated and remains open in the division of the anus, it will be easier for the patient. And sometimes the fistula is closed in this manner: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is at the side of the anus around the skin surface on the body and near the edge of the scrotum, then you take a sharp probe with perforated tip, similar to an awl for preparing coarse cloth in this form:
And he penetrates into that faithful envelope of five fields or around those areas; and he approaches the fistula, trying to reach its cavity until he achieves it.
If he penetrates into the margin of the anus closely, then you extract the feces from that wound so that you insert your finger into the anus; and extract the end of the feces and adjust both ends evenly, and tighten each one, and leave it for a day or two, and when the feces penetrates deeper into the flesh, tighten it within until those skins are incised which are between the ends of the feces and that they meet.
Then cure the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifices of the fistula are not penetrating, make it penetrate in any way you prepare, except that it is not too wide because it should not injure the ligament; and approach it until it is healed.
The method of spine-shaped spatula for dividing the fistula: the curvature of which is very sharp and the other part is not sharp, so that it does not injure anything unnecessary, as sometimes happens.
Stitching hemorrhoids, where blood flows during the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds, for they can be in the anus like coal or as if it were a mass of fat. And the small and large ones are those which bleed constantly and are one, and the piles that are multiple, and are outside the anus, and at the ends of it.
But the ones that are outside the anus occur during months with little moisture, from which a clear liquid or a small amount of blood with continuous flow comes out, and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of the one that is inside the anus is to command the patient to sit and to empty it before the anus becomes raw and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take and suspend with hooks or what you have those with your nail, and approach the incision of those, you should cut their roots.
But if the hooks are not present in those because of their moisture and softening of them, then take those with rough cloth or cotton or woolen gauze, remove those with your fingers, approach the incision of those and sprinkle some powders containing resins near the incision, to be used instead of cautery; or cauterize those according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterization. Then cure those with other treatment until they are healed.
And if the anus does not empty, then cauterize the patient with a small bite, and wash it with water that eases bowel movement when the patient squeezes.

Treatise on ulcers and fistulas.
Know that any wound or boil that becomes old and chronic, and does not heal and bleeds continuously without being cured, is universally referred to as a fistula and we call it an ulcer.
A fistula is a hard, nodular, white lesion that is not painful and has a concave shape like the shape of an ulcer caused by a bird's peck; for this reason it is called a cicatricial ulcer.
In a man with an ulcer that bleeds, the pus is often purged in some hours. Sometimes this pus becomes thickened, scanty, and slimy.
I have already shown all these causes, their symptoms and the treatment with medications in the classification.
And so, you should know that the healing of fistulas is done through surgical treatment with the hand.
You should know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body, as they reach large veins and arteries, nerves, spleen, intestines, bladder, one of the ribs, one of the vertebrae of the back, or one of the joints composed like the hand and foot; and those are the ones that provide proximity to the main member and similar areas.
Therefore, the fistula that occurs in this manner is one of the difficult-to-heal diseases and does not receive treatment, with the occupation being labor and ignorance.
If one of the fistulas has such depth that it does not reach the places mentioned and you hope for its healing and believe in its treatment, but wish to find out more about it, then take a probe or iron, and if the fistula is straight, use it to explore it.
If the fistula is twisted, then investigate it with lead wire, because lead has the property of lightness in its body and will alleviate and correct the twist.
If the fistula has horrible movements (spasms), it is not possible for you to probe it.
Therefore close the orifices with its own orifices, because the moisture that you use to close one will pass through the others and run out of them.
Then proceed with extreme care, for it is important to know if you have bone or nerve here, and whether the fistula is long or short, or if it is one that has horrible movements and is all around the entirety of your strength, your questioning, the examination of the patient, and the discovery of pain, you should use compression on the area with your hand and similar to the symptoms and causes of an abscess.

On extracting boils.
Boils are differentiated according to their species, and the areas of the body where they occur, as they have different shapes: some with large points, small, concave, sunken, solid ones; others with three angles, those that have tongues; and those that are stalks.
And as for the symptoms of the skull, when an arrow strikes it and passes through the bone, and exits at the base which is above the brain, this happens violently with headaches, blindness, dizziness, fever in the cheeks, inflammation and fever of the tongue, convulsions and confusion of thought, vomiting of bile, and the word is easily lost and the voice destroyed, and there is discharge from the wound of white pus similar to powder, and eyes like water from the flesh.
Therefore, if such symptoms appear to you, then do not attempt treatment or extraction of the arrow, unless it is necessary.
However, the symptoms of an arrow in the heart, which is near the left nipple and feels hard to touch, are not empty but filled; the movement of the arrow feels like the movement of a pulse, blood flows from the wound that is black, there is coldness at the extremities, excessive sweating, and fainting; therefore, you know that death approaches quickly.
The symptoms of an arrow in the lung are primarily sputum from the wound that is frothy blood, and the vessels near the neck are compressed, and the patient's complexion changes, and they breathe heavily and demand cold air.
If the arrow strikes the membrane located in the foot, and the pain is mainly in the small ribs, it causes severe pain with deep breathing and sighing, and not all of the member's muscles are affected.
If the arrow strikes the stomach, then a foul-smelling discharge comes from the wound.
If the arrow strikes the abdomen and is buried inside, there may be a hole in the wound, or tissues such as intestines or hernias that have been torn apart, and there is no hope for recovery from extraction of the arrow.
If the arrow strikes the bladder and comes out with urine, and there are signs of bleeding outside, and strong pain is felt by the patient, then you know that it is fatal.
However, other members such as the head, neck, throat, shoulders and joints, spine, cervical vertebrae, pelvis, hips, and their similar parts of the body can be saved if the arrow does not pierce a vein or artery and is not poisonous.
I recommend that you pay attention to the nature of these arrows, as this indicates the method of treatment.
The reason is that when an arrow hits a man in the tear duct of the eye at the root of the nose, and it is extracted from the other side, leaving the eyelash behind, healing occurs and no harm is done to the eye.

If we want to extract a lot of blood, scratch with deep scratching; if we know that the blood is thick, it is necessary to make a strong scratching.
The term "scratching" only refers to the depth of the incision.
If the incision is thick, hard, dark, and its pores are narrow, it is necessary that the sites of the swellings be lubricated with a more lenient and resolving oil; if it is in summer, for example with olive oil or violet oil, or sesame oil from coarse grain, or if it is in winter, use oil of garlic, oil of lily, camomile oil, or blood oil, and those similar.
If the excess is thick, fry oil of amaranth or balsam, oil of olive, oil of dill, and those similar.
But if the one who performs swelling has wide pores of tender skin, it is necessary that oil be prohibited, and it should be washed with water or hot water from solanum, or coarse grain water, or bitter water, and those similar to these.
And if the one whose blood is of great moisture, wash your swellings with vinegar or bitter water from myrtle and sumac and those similar.
And for that person whose superfluities are thick, wash their boils with old wine or water of roses, which is majorana, or decoction of anise, or camomile, and similar things.
It is necessary to keep the boil covered before washing it; it is necessary that it be administered immediately after washing for an hour or two, and it is necessary that they sleep near the boil.
It is necessary that the sandbag (ventosandus) be tied with a leech (phlebotomatus) before bloodletting (ventosationem).
It is necessary to consider at the beginning: if the person who will lance or is to perform bloodletting is choleric and has hot blood and inflammation, it is necessary that you take cooling substances, such as mustard, vinegar, lemons, and shallots, and bind them, and use julep and similar things.
Stop their food, such as potatoes, and meat from sparrows, and food seasoned with sour things, and similar things to them.
For that person whose complexion is cold, it is necessary to take elixir of almonds or elixir of anise seeds, sumac, and a moderately-scented spice between winter and spring; and it should be commanded to use little drink and eat less, and stop consuming potatoes, cabbage, fish, and small birds and doves.
And on the day of boil lancing and bloodletting, let them drink more than they eat.
And it should be given to drink in some hours alpharac tyrionic or musk medicine, that is musk, or celery before the boil lancing or bloodletting, or near them to comfort the main members and to make the blood thin; and it is not necessary for them to take that scald.
However, boils that are not incised are boils that are stopped in the liver, and on the spleen, and in the umbilicus, in the joints of the fingers, and the pit of the ankle, because these members cannot bear incision on them.
And it is not desired for those but the attraction of blood from a member, such as stopping a boil on the nipple in sickness of bleeding of the nose's blood; and they use that to dissolve cold and thickened boils in the member, such as stopping on the stomach and umbilicus; because that thins the member and scalds it, relieving pain, as it resolves boils.
And when it occurs in their opening or eruption, it is stopped on the nose because, by the strength of attraction, it weakens the opening and eradicates the eruption from its location.
And similarly, when it is stopped on the liver and spleen, boils are trapped in those locations.
These boils are administered with juice only, but some are administered with heat.
Some are administered full of boiling water in sickness of the spleen.
This is why the boil should be filled with pus and be large, which means boiling water alone or water in which appropriate herbs have been steeped.
The form of boil administered with heat: the width of the opening should be two fingers, according to how we have formed it; and the quantity of pus should be the size of a palm; and in the depth, in the location that is in the circumference, the depth should be the size of a finger, the hole should be small according to the quantity that can fit an awl.
Make a mixture of rose oil or lemon, large pieces of leon (possibly an old spelling for lion's tooth, a type of root), ginger and pepper to prevent the member from slipping from its position.
And let a thin transverse iron bar be placed over it (the affected area), on which a candle is held alight.
And this (plaster or poultice) should be much larger than the one we have recommended; and less in amount according to the severity of the illness and the state of the patient using it.
And (plasters or poultices for) children and weak people should be different from those of strong young adults.
The quality of applying this plaster with fire on the member is that it extends the meat with fire properly, but only a little bit of wax candle should be placed under it, and it should be placed on the middle of the transverse iron bar at the middle of the plaster, so that the fire is ignited around the edges to prevent burning the body of the patient.
And let it be applied to the member of the patient, and the hot plaster should be placed on top of the stick that we have mentioned, until when we have applied the plasters and do not need the heat and let the vapor rise over the stick, then the plaster will dissolve quickly.
And cook the meat according to its method, and repeat if necessary.
However, in the case of plaster for pleurisy (inflammation of the lining of the lungs), it is not applied with fire, as there is no transverse iron bar or stick. Instead, it is filled with water and applied only to the member (affected area).
And this is its form: The larger the plaster, the better, because it can receive more water.

Summary and collections of the nature of bone fractures, from which a preliminary is necessary before we begin the restoration of broken limbs and those of various types for each one. And know that when bones are fractured in men who are elderly or in the first youth, it is not possible for them to be continued and consolidated according to their nature due to the drying of their limbs.

Sign of fracture of the bone. By this is known the fracture of the bone: it is a deformity and prominence of the bone that can be felt, and it is that which you compress with your hand.
And therefore, if there is no apparent deformity or it is not felt when you touch the bone with movement and the patient does not feel much pain, then it is not a fracture here.
It is possible that there may be a deformity or small fissure, in which case you must press it with your hand and compress it completely; stop on the medicine of which there will be a reminder at this moment appropriate for the location; and apply tightness by gentle compression.
Know that the location which is arched and not divided into two or something else that does not occur in satiety, such as the entire circumference of its part, requires correction from your time of applying a cauterizing aposteme.

Chapter: On Fractures When They Occur in the Head.
The types of fractures are multiple, and the shapes of them are various, and their causes are distinct, because some fracture is caused by blunt force that breaks all the bone and leaves only the marrow as in the case of the thigh, and this type of fracture is called comminuted; or the blow cuts a part of the bone, and cuts through the flesh but does not pass beyond its surface; and this type of fracture is called absolute levation.
And the wound of these two types of fractures can be large or small, and the nature of the fracture is either contracted or stretched; and its cause is blunt force with a hammer or cudgel on stone, and their similar.
This fracture can either be penetrating and close to the panniculus which is left of the bone; or it can be on the face of the bone, and the wound of these two types of fractures can be large or small.
And a fracture that is narrowed in the bone, in its small hollow, and by this is called this type of fracture hairline.
A fracture that is caused by cudgel or blunt force on stone, which makes a layer of bone enter the joints inside, and occurs in the concave areas such as in the knees when it is struck and split open and enters into the joints inside.
And this occurs in soft bones like those of infants.
And all these types of fractures are treated similarly, like separate stars. I will return to the topic in its place.
We should be familiar with all these types of fractures through detection and investigation by probing and examination of rotten flesh that is on them.
The hairline fracture is recognized by this that it appears on the bone and is abscessed, then becomes thin over it through probing, because the fracture appears black.
In the treatment of fractures, consider at first the symptoms of the patient, and if you see through clear signs that they indicate fear, such as vomiting of bile, extension, loss of consciousness, abscesses in the mouth, fainting, acute fever, sores on the hands or redness of these areas, and similar symptoms in greater dispositions, do not doubt it is not healed.
If you see non-recurrent accidents (incidents), you hope for health, then you begin the treatment of it.
The cause is that if it is struck at the beginning as it is struck and that is in the days of winter, then it is necessary that you study the placement of the bone before the twelfth day according to all precautions.
And if it is in the summer days, then it is necessary that you remove the bone before the seventh day, knowing that what remains of the bone is rotten from the panniculus, and that the accidents that we have mentioned occur.
And if the fracture has reached the panniculus covering the brain, and is in small pieces and shattered, then it is necessary that you incise the fragmented and shattered parts, as I will advise you.
And it is that you shave the head of the struck patient, and expose the bone according to custom and your ability according to the figure of the injury, and it should be easy for the patient.
And if an accident occurs to you, you must detect the bone, drain blood or an abscess, then oppose yourself to it with what is necessary, and it is that you moisten the area with cloths soaked in wine and rose oil, make the injury rest until the abscess subsides, and ensure that there is no bleeding; and then begin with the circumnision of the bone and removal of it.

They are not called so, but rather that the stirrup does not reach the end of the bone from above, because at the tip of the stirrup is a round extremity or edge similar to a rim or small circle, which prohibits it from being submerged and passing through the thickness of the bone.
It is appropriate that you take a large number of these stirrups, the amount of which corresponds to the thickness of each bone, but only when it is present in all parts of the skull, the tip of which is sharp, the quantity in length and width should correspond to the thickness of the skull.
This is the form of three types of stirrups: The method of piercing around the broken bone is to place the stirrup on the bone and rotate it with your fingers until you know that the bone has been penetrated; and then move the stirrup to another location, and stop at a point where the total thickness of the ray or environment is reached.
Then incise the bone using incision tools between each crack, making it as thin as possible at the end of the cut, as we have said, until you extract the bone, or with your hand, or with some other cause by means of certain instruments that you will prepare for this, such as tweezers and forceps.
